[4:0:344,445] Legislative, Judicial, and Executive section of the  

[4:1:344,455] Governor's Budget are either established as  

[4:2:344,465] independent entities under the California  

[5:0:344,475] Constitution, or are departments with a recognized  

[5:1:344,485] need to operate outside of the administrative  

[5:2:344,495] oversight and control of an agency secretary.  

[5:3:344,505] Constitutionally-established bodies include the  

[5:4:344,515] Legislature, Judicial Branch, Governor's Office,  

[5:5:344,525] and constitutional officers. This section also  

[6:0:344,534] includes such independent entities as the Office of  

[6:1:344,544] the Inspector General and the California State  

[6:2:344,554] Lottery Commission.

[1:0:268,39] 0110   Senate  

[2:0:66,60] The Legislature is comprised of two houses, the Senate and the Assembly, and is responsible for enacting laws and  

[2:1:66,70] establishing public policy for California. The State Senate is comprised of 40 members who are elected for 4-year terms.  

[2:2:66,79] Members of the Legislature may serve a maximum of 12 years total in the Senate, the Assembly, or both, in any combination of  

[2:3:66,89] terms. Members first elected before June 6, 2012, however, may generally serve a maximum of 14 years total, with no more  

[2:4:66,99] than two terms in the Senate and three terms in the Assembly.

[11:0:66,463] The Legislature is comprised of two houses, the Senate and the Assembly, and is responsible for enacting laws and  

[11:1:66,473] establishing public policy for California. Both houses contribute to support the Legislative Analyst's Office, which provides fiscal  

[11:2:66,483] and policy advice to the Legislature, and is overseen by the 16-member bipartisan Joint Legislative Budget Committee.  

[11:3:66,500] Because the Legislature's   programs drive a need for infrastructure investment, the Legislature has a capital outlay program to  

[11:4:66,510] support this need.   For the specifics on the Legislature's   capital outlay program see "Infrastructure Overview."

[15:0:66,610] INFRASTRUCTURE OVERVIEW  

[16:0:66,628] The California State Capitol, which serves as the state’s working seat of government, began construction in 1860 and was  

[16:1:66,638] completed in 1874. The Capitol remained largely unchanged until 1949, when additional space requirements drove the need for  

[16:2:66,648] construction of the Capitol Annex, which attaches to the east side of the original Capitol building.   The Annex, which was  

[16:3:66,658] completed in 1951, houses legislative offices, committee rooms, and the Governor’s offices.  

[16:4:66,675] Government Code Section 9112(a) authorizes the Joint Rules Committee to pursue the construction of a new, restored,  

[16:5:66,685] rehabilitated, renovated, or reconstructed capitol building annex and associated projects.

[9:0:139,366] 0150   Contributions to the Legislators' Retirement System  

[10:0:66,387] Established in 1947, the Legislators' Retirement System provides retirement and death benefits for legislators, constitutional  

[10:1:66,397] officers, and legislative statutory officers.  

[11:0:66,416] The California Public Employees' Retirement System (CalPERS) administers the Legislators' Retirement System on behalf of  

[11:1:66,426] its members. Retirement benefits paid are based upon age, years of service, and final compensation. Benefits for death,  

[11:2:66,436] disability, and surviving dependents of deceased members are also provided under specific conditions.   The Legislators'  

[11:3:66,445] Retirement System is funded through contributions from the state, members of the system, and investment earnings. 

[12:0:66,465] Proposition 140, approved by voters in 1990, closed the Legislators' Retirement System to all new legislators after November  

[12:1:66,475] 6, 1990.   Subsequently, the California Public Employees' Pension Reform Act of 2013, Chapter 296, Statutes of 2012 (AB 340)  

[12:2:66,485] closed the Legislators' Retirement System to all new members effective January 1, 2013. New constitutional officers, statutory  

[12:3:66,494] officers, Sergeant-at-Arms, and the Insurance Commissioner retain optional membership rights in CalPERS.

[6:0:208,199] 0160   Legislative Counsel Bureau  

[7:0:66,220] The Legislative Counsel Bureau (Bureau) provides legal services to the two houses of the Legislature, and their members and  

[7:1:66,230] committees, by resolving a large volume of complex legal problems arising in connection with the legislative process. The legal  

[7:2:66,239] services furnished include rendering legal opinions, drafting bills and other legislative measures, counseling, attending  

[7:3:66,249] meetings of legislative committees as counsel, and representing the Legislature in litigation. The Bureau also provides legal  

[7:4:66,259] services to the Governor and advises state agencies as to the preparation of legislative measures. An attorney-client  

[7:5:66,269] relationship is maintained and all work is confidential.  

[8:0:66,288] In addition, the Bureau prepares and provides necessary indices and appropriate tables necessary to identify legislative  

[8:1:66,298] measures and compiles and indexes statutes and codes.  

[9:0:66,318] The Bureau operates the Legislative Data Center, which provides technology services to the Legislature, including IT services  

[9:1:66,327] in support of legislative business operations and the legislative information system, which provides information to the public  

[9:2:66,337] regarding pending legislation and existing law.  

[10:0:66,357] Pursuant to Chapter 46 of the Statutes of 2012, the California Commission on Uniform State Laws was transferred into the  

[10:1:66,366] Bureau. The California Commission on Uniform State Laws presents to the Legislature uniform laws recommended by the  

[10:2:66,376] National Conference of Commissioners on Uniform State Laws and then promotes passage of these uniform acts.  

[10:3:66,393] Pursuant to Chapter 450 of the Statutes of 2018, the Bureau provides advice and investigation services to the Legislature  

[10:4:66,403] related to workplace misconduct through the Workplace Conduct Unit.

[9:0:242,409] 0250   Judicial Branch  

[10:0:66,430] Article VI of the Constitution creates the Supreme Court of California and the Courts of Appeal to exercise the judicial power of  

[10:1:66,440] the state at the appellate level. Article VI also creates the Judicial Council of California to administer the state's judicial system.  

[10:2:66,450] Chapter 869, Statutes of 1997, created the California Habeas Corpus Resource Center to represent any person financially  

[10:3:66,460] unable to employ appellate counsel in capital cases.  

[11:0:66,479] The Lockyer-Isenberg Trial Court Funding Act of 1997 (Chapter 850, Statutes of 1997) provided a stable and consistent  

[11:1:66,489] funding source for the trial courts. Beginning with fiscal year 1997-98, consolidation of the costs of trial court operation was  

[11:2:66,499] implemented at the state level, with the exception of facility, revenue collection, and local judicial benefit costs. This  

[12:0:66,508] implementation capped the counties' general purpose revenue contributions to trial court costs at a revised 1994-95 level. The  

[12:1:66,518] county contributions become part of the Trial Court Trust Fund, which supports all trial court operations. Fine and penalty  

[12:2:66,528] revenue collected by each county is retained or distributed in accordance with statute. Each county makes quarterly payments  

[12:3:66,538] to the Trial Court Trust Fund equal to the fine and penalty revenue received by the state General Fund in 1994-95, as adjusted  

[12:4:66,548] by amounts equivalent to specified fine and fee revenues that counties benefited from in 2003-04. The Trial Court Facilities Act  

[12:5:66,557] of 2002 (Chapter 1082, statutes of 2002) provided a process for the responsibility for court facilities to be transferred from the  

[12:6:66,567] counties to the state by July 1, 2007, which was extended to December 31, 2009, by Chapter 9, Statutes of 2008. The Trial  

[12:7:66,577] Court Facilities Act of 2002 also established several new revenue sources, effective on January 1, 2003. These revenues are  

[12:8:66,587] deposited into the State Court Facilities Construction Fund for the purpose of funding the construction and maintenance of  

[12:9:66,596] court facilities throughout the state. Counties contribute revenues for the ongoing operation and maintenance of court facilities  

[12:10:66,606] based upon historical expenditures for facilities transferred to the state.  

[13:0:66,626] The mission of the Judicial Branch is to resolve disputes arising under the law and to interpret and apply the law consistently,  

[13:1:66,636] impartially, and independently to protect the rights and liberties guaranteed by the Constitutions of California and the United  

[13:2:66,645] States, in a fair, accessible, effective, and efficient manner.  

[14:0:66,665] Because the Judicial Branch's programs drive a need for infrastructure investment, the Judicial Branch has a capital outlay  

[14:1:66,675] program to support this need. For   the specifics on   the Judicial Branch's capital outlay program, see "Infrastructure Overview."  

[15:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[0:0:66,13] LEGISLATIVE, JUDICIAL, AND EXECUTIVE 

[1:0:414,13] 2024-25 STATE BUDGET — LJE   21 

[2:0:207,32] 0250   Judicial Branch - Continued 

[3:0:66,65] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[3:1:66,84] 0130 - SUPREME COURT  

[4:0:66,103] The Supreme Court is the highest court in the California judicial system. Its decisions are binding on all other California state  

[4:1:66,113] courts. The Chief Justice of California and the six Associate Justices entertain petitions seeking review of decisions from the  

[4:2:66,123] Courts of Appeal, original petitions for extraordinary relief (such as writs of mandate or habeas corpus), and recommendations  

[4:3:66,133] for discipline of judicial officers and attorneys. The Court grants review and issues opinions in order to settle legal questions of  

[4:4:66,142] statewide importance. In addition, under the California Constitution, all death penalty judgments are appealed directly to the  

[4:5:66,152] Supreme Court.  

[4:6:66,169] 0135 - COURTS OF APPEAL  

[5:0:66,189] Established by a constitutional amendment in 1904, the Courts of Appeal are California's intermediate courts of review. The six  

[5:1:66,199] District Courts of Appeal hear appeals and original proceedings at nine different locations around the state. Cases before the  

[5:2:66,209] Courts of Appeal involve every area of civil and criminal law.  

[5:3:66,226] 0140 - JUDICIAL COUNCIL  

[6:0:66,245] The Judicial Council of California is the constitutional policy-making body for the state judiciary. The Council consists of 21  

[6:1:66,255] voting members and 9 advisory members; the Chief Justice of California serves as chair. The Judicial Council staff serve as the  

[6:2:66,265] administrative arm of the Council. Staff provide policy support to the Council, administrative accountability in the operation of  

[6:3:66,275] the courts as specified by law, strategic planning for capital outlay, design, and construction of court facilities; and  

[6:4:66,284] administrative support for courts in areas such as budget, fiscal services, coordination of the assignment of retired judges,  

[6:5:66,294] technology, education, legal advice and services, human resources, legislative advocacy, and research.  

[6:6:66,312] 0140023 - JUDICIAL BRANCH FACILITY PROGRAM  

[7:0:66,331] The Judicial Branch Facility Program administers the acquisition, planning, construction, operations, and maintenance of  

[7:1:66,341] judicial branch facilities. This program is responsible for the development of long-term facilities master plans, facility and real  

[7:2:66,351] estate management, renovation of existing court facilities, and new courthouse planning, design, and construction.  

[7:3:66,368] 0150 - STATE TRIAL COURT FUNDING  

[8:0:66,385] California has 58 trial courts, one in each county. In trial courts, or superior courts, a judge and sometimes a jury hears  

[8:1:66,395] witnesses' testimony and other evidence and decides cases by applying the relevant law to the facts.   Trial courts have trial  

[8:2:66,405] jurisdiction over all criminal and civil cases. To accomplish various statutory mandates, the State Trial Court Funding Program  

[8:3:66,414] supports trial courts through the following programs:  

[8:4:66,434] 0150010 - SUPPORT FOR THE OPERATION OF THE TRIAL COURTS  

[9:0:66,451] This program's objective is to provide the resources necessary for the statewide trial court system to adjudicate civil and  

[9:1:66,461] criminal cases. This program includes all allowable trial court administrative costs under Government Code section 77003.  

[9:2:66,478] 0150011 - COURT APPOINTED DEPENDENCY COUNSEL  

[10:0:66,496] This program provides funding for court-appointed counsel for children, non-minor dependents and parents in juvenile court  

[10:1:66,505] dependency proceedings pursuant to Welfare and Institutions Code section 317, subdivisions (b) and (c), and Government  

[10:2:66,515] Code section 77003, subdivision (a)(4).  

[10:3:66,532] 0150019 - COMPENSATION OF SUPERIOR COURT JUDGES  

[10:4:66,550] This program provides funding for the salaries and state benefits for Superior Court judges.  

[10:5:66,567] 0150028 - ASSIGNED JUDGES  

[11:0:66,584] This program provides support for the salaries and related costs of retired as well as active judges who are assigned by the  

[11:1:66,594] Chief Justice to positions in courts which require assistance due to judicial absences or other factors impacting the ability of a  

[11:2:66,604] court to avoid case delay.  

[11:3:66,621] 0150037 - COURT INTERPRETERS  

[12:0:66,638] This program supports the provision of qualified language interpreters in criminal, juvenile, family, mental competency,  

[12:1:66,648] Community Assistance, Recovery, and Empowerment (CARE) Act, and civil proceedings as required by statute.  

[12:2:66,665] 0150046 - GRANTS  

[13:0:66,683] This program provides funding for government grants providing public services related to the trial courts.  

[13:1:66,700] 0150051 – CHILD SUPPORT COMMISSIONER PROGRAM (AB 1058)  

[14:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[0:0:66,13] 2024-25 STATE BUDGET — LJE   22 

[1:0:382,13] LEGISLATIVE, JUDICIAL, AND EXECUTIVE 

[2:0:207,32] 0250   Judicial Branch - Continued 

[3:0:66,68] This program provides funding for Child Support Commissioners and Family Law Facilitators in every court.  

[3:1:66,86] 0150067 – COURT APPOINTED SPECIAL ADVOCATE (CASA) PROGRAM  

[4:0:66,103] This program provides funding for non-profits designated by the court to train and provide volunteers to advocate for children in  

[4:1:66,113] foster care.  

[4:2:66,130] 0150083 – EQUAL ACCESS FUND  

[5:0:66,147] This program provides funding to the Legal Services Trust Fund Commission of the State Bar of California to fund for legal  

[5:1:66,157] services programs to providing a range of services to low-income litigants.  

[5:2:66,174] 0150095 - EXPENSES ON BEHALF OF THE TRIAL COURT  

[6:0:66,192] This program provides appropriation for statewide programs and services provided to the court or courts by the Judicial Council  

[6:1:66,201] or payment for services or property of any kind contracted for the court or courts or on behalf of the courts by the Judicial  

[6:2:66,211] Council, which are paid for or reimbursed by the trial courts. The appropriation also supports the implementation and  

[6:3:66,221] administration of the Sargent Shriver Civil Counsel Pilot Program.  

[7:0:66,248] In addition to the programs mentioned above, the State Trial Court Funding Program supports Children in Dependency Cases  

[7:1:66,258] Training.  

[8:0:66,275] 0155 - HABEAS CORPUS RESOURCE CENTER  

[9:0:66,295] The Habeas Corpus Resource Center provides legal representation for indigent petitioners in death penalty habeas corpus  

[9:1:66,304] proceedings before the California state courts and the federal courts. The Center also serves as a resource center for the  

[9:2:66,314] private capital defense bar, and it   recruits and trains attorneys to expand the pool of private counsel qualified to accept  

[9:3:66,324] appointments in death penalty habeas corpus proceedings,   and thereby helps to reduce the number of unrepresented indigents  

[9:4:66,334] on California's death row.

[5:0:66,211] INFRASTRUCTURE OVERVIEW  

[6:0:66,230] The Judicial Branch consists of the Supreme Court, courts of appeal, trial courts, and the Judicial Council. The Supreme Court  

[6:1:66,239] is located in the Civic Center Plaza in San Francisco and the Ronald Reagan State Building in Los Angeles and has office  

[6:2:66,249] space in San Diego. The courts of appeal are organized into six districts, operate in nine different locations, and consist of  

[6:3:66,259] approximately 538,000 sf. The trial courts are located in 58 counties statewide, in approximately 430 facilities, and 2,200  

[6:4:66,269] courtrooms of approximately 16 million sf of usable area and more than 21.8 million sf of space under Judicial Council  

[6:5:66,278] responsibility, management, and part of the overall portfolio. The facilities of the Supreme Court, courts of appeal, and trial  

[6:6:66,288] courts encompass not only the public courtroom spaces but also the chambers and workspaces where judicial officers and  

[6:7:66,298] courtroom staff prepare for proceedings; secure areas, including holding cells; and building support functions. Judicial Council  

[6:8:66,308] administrative facilities, occupying approximately 253,000 sf, are located in San Francisco and Sacramento.

[5:0:180,218] 0280   Commission on Judicial Performance  

[6:0:66,239] The California Commission on Judicial Performance is the independent state agency responsible for investigating complaints of  

[6:1:66,249] judicial misconduct and judicial incapacity, and for disciplining judges pursuant to Article VI, Section 18 of the California  

[6:2:66,259] Constitution. It is the only body with such authority in the state. Its jurisdiction includes all active judges and justices of  

[6:3:66,268] California's superior courts, Courts of Appeal and Supreme Court, and former judges for conduct prior to retirement or  

[6:4:66,278] resignation. The Commission also shares authority with the local courts for the oversight of court commissioners and referees.  

[6:5:66,288] In addition to its disciplinary functions, the Commission is responsible for handling judges' applications for disability retirement.  

[7:0:66,307] The Commission's authority is limited to investigating alleged judicial misconduct and, if warranted, imposing discipline. Judicial  

[7:1:66,317] misconduct usually involves conduct in conflict with the standards set forth in the Code of Judicial Ethics. After investigation  

[7:2:66,327] and, in some cases a public hearing, the Commission may impose sanctions ranging from confidential discipline to removal  

[7:3:66,337] from office.  

[8:0:66,356] The Commission is composed of 11 members: 3 judges appointed by the Supreme Court; 2 attorneys appointed by the  

[8:1:66,366] Governor; and 6 lay citizens, of which 2 are appointed by the Governor, 2 are appointed by the Senate Committee on Rules,  

[8:2:66,376] and 2 are appointed by the Speaker of the Assembly. Members are appointed to four-year terms and may serve two terms.  

[8:3:66,386] Commission members do not receive a salary.

[9:0:150,349] 0390   Contributions to the Judges' Retirement System  

[10:0:66,370] The Judges' Retirement System provides retirement benefit funding for judges on California's Supreme, Appellate, and  

[10:1:66,379] Superior/Municipal courts. The California Public Employees' Retirement System administers both the Judges' Retirement  

[10:2:66,389] System and the Judges' Retirement System II on behalf of its members.  

[11:0:66,407] The Judges' Retirement System is closed to new members, and a second retirement system for judges was established in  

[11:1:66,416] 1994. All new judges elected or appointed on or after November 9, 1994 become members of the Judges' Retirement System  

[11:2:66,426] II. The Judges' Retirement System II provides retirement, disability, and death benefits based on age, years of service, final  

[11:3:66,436] compensation, and eligibility, as determined by specific sections of the Judges' Retirement System II Law. Judges' Retirement  

[11:4:66,446] System II members eligible for a service retirement have the option of choosing the monetary credit plan (a lump-sum return of  

[11:5:66,455] contributions and interest earned) or the defined benefit plan. Judges' Retirement System II members not eligible for a defined  

[11:6:66,465] benefit receive the balance of their monetary credits (in a lump-sum payment). The Judges' Retirement System II is funded  

[11:7:66,475] through contributions from the state, members of the system, and investment earnings. The state's contributions are adjusted  

[11:8:66,485] annually to maintain actuarial soundness of the fund.  

[12:0:66,504] The Judges' Retirement System provides retirement, disability, and death benefits based on age, years of service,  

[12:1:66,514] compensation of active judges, and eligibility, as determined by specific sections of the Judges' Retirement Law. Active judges  

[12:2:66,524] and the state each contribute 8 percent of salary to the Judges' Retirement System. Additional contributions come from filing  

[12:3:66,534] fees for specific civil cases and investment income. These contributions, however, are not sufficient to fully fund benefit  

[12:4:66,543] payments. Consequently, current law requires the state to fund the difference between existing contribution sources and the  

[12:5:66,553] required benefit payments to retired judges.  

[13:0:66,573] Effective January 1, 2013, provisions of the California Public Employees' Pension Reform Act of 2013, Chapter 296, Statutes of  

[13:1:66,582] 2012 (AB 340), require that new judges contribute 50 percent of the normal cost of their pension benefits.

[4:0:66,428] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[4:1:66,447] 0220 - GO-Biz  

[5:0:66,466] The GO-Biz serves as the Governor's lead entity for economic strategy and the marketing of California on issues relating to  

[5:1:66,476] business development, private sector investment, and economic growth, and export promotion. This program makes  

[5:2:66,486] recommendations to the Governor and the Legislature regarding policies, programs, and actions to advance statewide  

[5:3:66,496] economic goals.  

[6:0:66,513] 0225 - CALIFORNIA BUSINESS INVESTMENT SERVICES  

[7:0:66,530] This program serves employers, corporate executives, business owners, and site location consultants who are considering  

[7:1:66,540] California for business investment and expansion. This program convenes teams on key business development issues. This  

[7:2:66,550] program works with local, state, and federal partners to attract, retain, and grow businesses in addition to providing permit  

[7:3:66,559] assistance and helping businesses succeed in California.  

[7:4:66,577] 0230 - CALIFORNIA OFFICE OF THE SMALL BUSINESS ADVOCATE  

[8:0:66,594] The California Office of the Small Business Advocate (CalOSBA) serves as the principal advocate in the state on behalf of  

[8:1:66,604] small businesses, including legislation and administrative regulations that affect small business. CalOSBA ensures that  

[8:2:66,614] information, content and direct support are available to minority and small businesses to better navigate state resources,  

[8:3:66,623] programs and services. CalOSBA advocates on behalf of small businesses concerning the actions of state agencies, state  

[8:4:66,633] laws, regulations and procurement opportunities, maintaining the connection to agency small business advocates/liaisons. It  

[8:5:66,643] serves as the co-Coordinator with CalOES for the Economic Recovery Support Function under the California Disaster  

[8:6:66,653] Recovery Framework. CalOSBA administers the Technical Assistance Expansion Program and Capital Infusion Program grants  

[8:7:66,662] for support services to underserved business groups, as well as the Innovation Hub (iHub) and CA Made programs.  

[8:8:66,680] 0235010 - CALIFORNIA FILM COMMISSION  

[9:0:66,697] The California Film Commission (CFC) enhances California's status as the leader in motion picture, television and commercial  

[9:1:66,707] production. The Commission is tasked with retaining and increasing motion picture production and to see that it continues to  

[10:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[3:0:66,68] create jobs and boost business throughout the State. A one-stop office for filmmakers, the Commission supports productions of  

[3:1:66,78] all sizes and budgets with a variety of services. In addition to issuing film permits for all state properties, administering the film  

[3:2:66,88] and TV tax credit program, maintaining an extensive location library, and offering production assistance on a wide variety of  

[3:3:66,98] issues, CFC also works closely with cities and counties with the goal of creating 'film friendly" policies that are consistent state-

[3:4:66,108] wide.  

[4:0:66,125] 0235019 - DIVISION OF TOURISM  

[5:0:66,142] The California Tourism Market Act provides for the marketing of California through an assessment of businesses that benefit  

[5:1:66,152] from travel and tourism. The objective of the Tourism Assessment Program is to identify potentially assessable businesses,  

[5:2:66,162] assist companies with determining the appropriate amount of their self-assessment, and collet the fee.  

[6:0:66,179] 0235028 - CALIFORINIA INFRASTRUCTURE AND ECONOMIC DEVELOPMENT BANK  

[7:0:66,196] California Infrastructure and Economic Development Bank (IBank) was created to finance public infrastructure and private  

[7:1:66,206] development that promote a healthy climate for jobs, contribute to a strong economy and improve the quality of life in California  

[7:2:66,216] communities. IBank has broad authority to participate in a variety of financing transactions, including issuing tax-exempt and  

[7:3:66,226] taxable revenue bonds, providing financing to a variety of entities, providing credit enhancements, acquiring or leasing facilities,  

[7:4:66,235] and leveraging State and Federal funds. IBank's current programs include the infrastructure state revolving fund program (ISRF  

[7:5:66,245] Program), the California lending for energy and environmental needs center (CLEEN Center, a sub-program of the ISRF  

[7:6:66,255] Program), the statewide energy and efficiency program and the light emitting diode street lighting program (each a component  

[7:7:66,265] of the CLEEN Center), the bond financing program, which issues 501(c)(3)tax-exempt and taxable bonds,, industrial  

[7:8:66,274] development revenue bonds, exempt facility revenue bonds, and public agency revenue bonds.  

[8:0:66,292] 0235037 - SMALL BUSINESS LOAN GUARANTEE PROGRAM  

[9:0:66,309] The Small Business Loan Guarantee Program (SBLGP) promotes local economic development by providing guarantees for  

[9:1:66,319] loans issued to small businesses from financial institutions, typically banks, that otherwise would not approve a term loan or  

[9:2:66,329] line of credit to a small business. As a result of the SBLGP, participating small businesses are able to secure financing that  

[9:3:66,338] allows them to grow and expand their business. The loan guarantee serves as a credit enhancement and an incentive for  

[9:4:66,348] financial institutions to make loans to small businesses that otherwise would not be eligible for such financing.  

[10:0:66,365] 0235046 - CALIFORNIA WELCOME CENTERS  

[11:0:66,383] California Welcome Centers are visitor information centers that are readily accessible to and recognizable by tourists to  

[11:1:66,392] encourage tourism in California and provide benefits to the state economy. The objective of the California Welcome Center  

[11:2:66,402] Program is to determine the locality of underserved travelers, designate a welcome center, and establish operating standards  

[11:3:66,412] across the network.  

[12:0:66,429] 0240 - CALIFORNIA COMMUNITY REINVESTMENT GRANT PROGRAM 

[13:0:66,446] The California Community Reinvestment Grants (CalCRG) Program   was established on July 1, 2018   to   implement the  

[13:1:66,456] competitive grant program mandated by Proposition 64, the Adult Use of Marijuana Act, and the provisions specified in  

[13:2:66,466] Revenue and Taxation Code section 34019(d).   The CalCRG Program administers grants   for   local public   health departments  

[13:3:66,476] and qualified community-based nonprofit organizations to support various mental health treatment, substance use treatment,  

[13:4:66,486] job placement, legal services and other health and wellness-related programs for communities disproportionately affected by  

[13:5:66,495] past federal and state drug policies in California. GO-Biz must award grants annually and at least 50 percent of the grant  

[13:6:66,505] funding will be allocated to qualified community-based nonprofit organizations.  

[14:0:66,522] 0245 - LOCAL EQUITY GRANT PROGRAM  

[15:0:66,540] The Local Equity Grant Program, administered by the Governor’s Office of Business and Economic Development, will assist  

[15:1:66,549] local equity applicants or local equity licensees pursuant to subparagraphs (A) through (C), inclusive, of paragraph (2) of  

[15:2:66,559] subdivision (b) of Section 26244 of the Business and Professions Code.

[9:0:66,427] The Business, Consumer Services, and Housing Agency (Agency) is responsible for overseeing departments, boards,  

[9:1:66,436] commissions, panels, and agencies that provide the following services to the people of California: protection of the public  

[9:2:66,446] through the licensing and regulation of more than   4 million professionals, businesses, financial services and state-licensed  

[9:3:66,456] financial institutions; enforcement of the sale of alcoholic beverages and cannabis; regulation of the horse-racing industry;  

[9:4:66,466] regulating, funding and facilitating the preservation and expansion of safe, affordable housing; advancing statewide  

[9:5:66,475] collaborative efforts to provide funding and services to prevent and end homelessness; and guarding and enforcing California’s  

[9:6:66,485] civil rights laws. The Agency is comprised of the following entities: the Department of Alcoholic Beverage Control, the  

[9:7:66,495] Department of Cannabis Control, the Department of Consumer Affairs, the Department of Financial Protection and Innovation,  

[9:8:66,505] the Department of Real Estate, the California Housing Finance Agency, the Department of Housing and Community  

[9:9:66,515] Development, the Civil Rights Department, the Alcoholic Beverage Control Appeals Board, the Cannabis Control Appeals  

[9:10:66,524] Panel, the California Horse Racing Board, and the California Interagency Council on Homelessness.

[5:0:66,211] The Administration of the Transportation Agency, under direction of the Secretary, advises the Governor on major policy and  

[5:1:66,221] program matters and provides oversight and support of the Agency's departments and programs.  

[5:2:66,238] 0275 - CALIFORNIA TRAFFIC SAFETY PROGRAM  

[6:0:66,258] The California Traffic Safety Program develops the California Highway Safety Plan. The plan uses available state and federal  

[6:1:66,268] resources to identify and address major traffic safety problems throughout the state.  

[6:2:66,285] 0276 - TRANSIT AND INTERCITY RAIL CAPITAL PROGRAM  

[7:0:66,305] The Transit and Intercity Rail Capital Program provides grants to encourage low carbon transit operations through the Transit,  

[7:1:66,314] Affordable Housing, and Sustainable Communities Program. The program goals include reducing greenhouse gas emissions,  

[7:2:66,324] improving mobility access across the state, and providing benefits to California's disadvantaged communities.  

[7:3:66,341] 0277 - STATEWIDE TRANSPORTATION PRIORITIES  

[8:0:66,359] The Statewide Transportation Priorities program provides grant funding to address California’s long-term transportation goals  

[8:1:66,368] by improving California’s transportation system and helping California achieve its climate goals.

[7:1:66,357] The primary mission of the Health and Human Services Agency (CalHHS) is to provide policy leadership and direction to the  

[7:2:66,367] departments, board and programs it oversees, to reduce duplication and fragmentation among CalHHS departments in policy  

[7:3:66,377] development and implementation, to improve coordination among departments on common programs, to ensure programmatic  

[7:4:66,387] integrity, and to advance the Governor's priorities on health and human services issues.  

[8:0:66,406] The CalHHS accomplishes its mission through the administration and coordination of state and federal programs for public  

[8:1:66,416] health, health care services, social services, public assistance, health planning and licensing, rehabilitation, and health  

[8:2:66,426] workforce development. These programs touch the lives of millions of California's most needy and vulnerable residents. The  

[8:3:66,435] CalHHS is committed to striking a balance between maintaining access to essential health and human services for California's  

[8:4:66,445] most disadvantaged and at-risk residents while pursuing ways to better manage and control costs.

[6:0:66,450] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[6:1:66,468] 0280 - SECRETARY FOR HEALTH AND HUMAN SERVICES  

[7:0:66,488] The Secretary for California Health and Human Services Agency provides the Governor with the highest level of advice on  

[7:1:66,498] state health, human services and related budget policy issues. The Secretary also provides the highest level of leadership and  

[7:2:66,507] oversight of the agency-wide efforts to promote the health and well-being of a growing and increasingly diverse California  

[7:3:66,517] population.  

[8:0:66,535] 0285 - THE CALIFORNIA OFFICE OF HEALTH INFORMATION INTEGRITY  

[9:0:66,554] The California Office of Health Information Integrity (CalOHII) is responsible for statewide leadership, coordination, policy  

[9:1:66,564] formation, direction, and oversight responsibilities for federal Health Insurance Portability and Accountability Act (HIPAA)  

[9:2:66,574] requirements. As the leading resource for providing HIPAA expertise to the State of California, CalOHII exercises full authority  

[9:3:66,583] relative to state entities to establish policy, provide direction to state entities, monitor progress and report on implementation  

[9:4:66,593] efforts based on state and federal laws.  

[9:5:66,610] 0286 - OFFICE OF YOUTH AND COMMUNITY RESTORATION  

[9:6:66,628] The mission for the Office of Youth and Community Restoration is to support the transition of justice involved youth to be  

[9:7:66,637] served in local communities and promote trauma responsive, culturally informed services for youth involved in the juvenile  

[9:8:66,647] justice system that support the youths’ successful transition into adulthood and help them become responsible, thriving, and  

[9:9:66,657] engaged members of their communities.  

[9:10:66,674] 0290 - OFFICE OF TECHNOLOGY AND SOLUTIONS INTEGRATION  

[10:0:66,694] The Office of Technology and Solutions Integration's (OTSI) mission is to procure, manage, and deliver complex technology  

[10:1:66,704] systems that support the delivery of health and human services for automation projects for the Health and Human Services  

[11:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[4:6:66,271] 0295 - OFFICE OF THE PATIENT ADVOCATE  

[5:0:66,288] The mission of the Office of the Patient Advocate is to improve the access to and quality of health care services by promoting  

[5:1:66,298] transparency and accountability. The Office of the Patient Advocate is mandated to produce a number of public reports on  

[5:2:66,307] health care service topics. Current reporting activities include:

[5:6:76,366] providers, and  

[6:0:65,382] • Model protocols for State Consumer Assistance Call Centers.  

[6:1:66,399] 0296 - CENTER FOR DATA INSIGHTS AND INNOVATION  

[7:0:66,416] The mission of the Center for Data Insights and Innovation is to improve the lives of all Californians by turning data into  

[7:1:66,426] insights, knowledge and action to increase the efficiency and utilization of data in the promotion of person-centered, data-driven  

[7:2:66,436] decision making, and integrated care and services.  

[7:3:66,453] 0297 - OFFICE OF THE SURGEON GENERAL  

[8:0:66,470] The position of the California Surgeon General was established to bring heightened attention to upstream factors that influence  

[8:1:66,480] chronic and acute conditions, advise the Governor, and serve as a leading spokesperson on matters of public health.  

[8:2:66,490] Specifically, the office is responsible for (a) Raising public awareness on and coordinating policies governing scientific  

[8:3:66,500] screening and treatment for toxic stress and adverse childhood experiences (ACEs); (b) Advising the Governor, the Secretary  

[8:4:66,509] of the California Health and Human Services Agency, and policymakers on a comprehensive approach to address health  

[8:5:66,519] issues and challenges focused on health equity, early childhood development, and ACEs and toxic stress; (c) Marshalling the  

[8:6:66,529] insights and energy of medical professionals, scientists, and other academic and public health experts, public servants, and  

[8:7:66,539] everyday Californians to solve our most pressing health challenges.

[9:0:164,407] 0540   Secretary of the Natural Resources Agency  

[10:0:66,428] The mission of the Natural Resources Agency is to restore, protect and manage the state's natural, historical and cultural  

[10:1:66,438] resources for current and future generations using creative approaches and solutions based on science, collaboration and  

[10:2:66,448] respect for all involved communities. The Secretary for Natural Resources, a member of the Governor's Cabinet, sets the  

[10:3:66,457] policies and coordinates the environmental preservation and restoration activities of 27 various departments, boards,  

[10:4:66,467] commissions and conservancies, and directly administers the Sea Grant Program, Ocean Protection Council, California  

[10:5:66,477] Environmental Quality Act, Environmental Enhancement Mitigation Program, River Parkways, Urban Greening, and the  

[10:6:66,487] California Cultural and Historical Endowment grant programs.  

[11:0:66,506] The Natural Resources Agency consists of the departments of Forestry and Fire Protection, Conservation, Fish and Wildlife,  

[11:1:66,516] Parks and Recreation, and Water Resources; the California Conservation Corps; Exposition Park; California Science Center;  

[11:2:66,526] California African American Museum; Office of Energy Infrastructure Safety; the State Lands Commission; the Colorado River  

[11:3:66,535] Board; the San Francisco Bay Conservation and Development Commission; the Energy Resources Conservation and  

[11:4:66,545] Development Commission; the Wildlife Conservation Board; the Delta Protection Commission; the California Coastal  

[11:5:66,555] Commission; the State Coastal Conservancy; the California Tahoe Conservancy; the Santa Monica Mountains Conservancy;  

[11:6:66,565] the Coachella Valley Mountains Conservancy; the San Joaquin River Conservancy; the San Gabriel and Lower Los Angeles  

[11:7:66,575] Rivers and Mountains Conservancy; the Baldwin Hills Conservancy; the San Diego River Conservancy; the Sierra Nevada  

[11:8:66,584] Conservancy; the Sacramento-San Joaquin Delta Conservancy; the Native American Heritage Commission; and the Special  

[11:9:66,594] Resources Program.

[12:0:199,567] 0552   Office of the Inspector General  

[13:0:66,588] The Office of the Inspector General (OIG) protects public safety by safeguarding the integrity of California's correctional  

[13:1:66,598] system. OIG is responsible for providing contemporaneous oversight of the California Department of Corrections and  

[13:2:66,608] Rehabilitation's (CDCR) internal affairs investigations, use of force, staff complaints, and the employee disciplinary process.  

[13:3:66,618] The Inspector General audits and reviews the policies, practices, and procedures of CDCR. The Inspector General reviews the  

[13:4:66,627] Governor's candidates for appointment to serve as warden for the state's adult correctional institutions and conducts metric-

[13:5:66,637] oriented inspection programs to periodically review delivery of medical care at each state prison. OIG receives communications  

[13:6:66,647] from individuals alleging improper governmental activity and maintains a toll-free public telephone number to receive  

[13:7:66,657] allegations of wrongdoing by employees of CDCR; conducts formal reviews of complaints of retaliation from CDCR employees  

[13:8:66,666] against upper management where a legally cognizable cause of action is present; and reviews sexual abuse incidents within  

[13:9:66,676] correctional institutions. OIG provides critical public transparency for the state correctional system by publicly reporting its  

[13:10:66,686] findings.

[13:0:175,620] 0555   Secretary for Environmental Protection  

[14:0:66,641] The Secretary for Environmental Protection is the cabinet-level agency responsible for protecting the environment. California  

[14:1:66,651] Environmental Protection Agency programs reduce greenhouse gas emissions, restore and protect environmental quality, and  

[14:2:66,661] protect public health. The Secretary coordinates the state's environmental regulatory programs and oversees the fair and  

[14:3:66,670] consistent enforcement of environmental law, which safeguards the state's residents and promotes the state's economic vitality.  

[14:4:66,680] The Secretary also administers environmental justice, environmental law enforcement, emergency preparedness and  

[14:5:66,690] response, Certified Unified Program Agencies, and scientific review programs. The Secretary leads greenhouse gas emission  

[14:6:66,700] reduction and climate change activities in state government, and is responsible for coordinating the implementation of Chapter  

[14:7:66,710] 488, Statutes of 2006 (AB 32). The Secretary also centralizes coordination of California-Mexico border environmental efforts.

[9:0:133,547] 0650   Governor’s Office of Land Use and Climate Innovation  

[10:0:66,568] The Governor’s Office of Land Use and Climate Innovation assists the Governor and the Administration in planning, research,  

[10:1:66,577] policy development, and legislative analysis. The Office formulates long-range state goals and policies to address key areas  

[10:2:66,587] related to climate, land use, and innovation: land use and planning, climate risk and resilience, environmental protection,  

[10:3:66,597] sustainable economic development, and targeted long-range research needs. The Office acts as the state's liaison to a variety  

[10:4:66,607] of entities including local and regional government, planning professionals, small business, academic institutions, tribal nations,  

[10:5:66,616] and the federal government. The Office also serves a role as convener across multiple state agencies on cross-cutting issues  

[10:6:66,626] in the four key areas of their work. 

[11:0:66,646] The Office includes two main budget programs: the State Planning and Policy Development that houses most of core planning  

[11:1:66,656] and research functions, as well as the Racial Equity Commission and the California Strategic Growth Council, which  

[11:2:66,665] coordinates and works collaboratively with public agencies, communities, and key partners to realize healthy, thriving, resilient  

[11:3:66,675] communities for all and provides direct grant funding to projects demonstrating the value and feasibility of sustainable  

[11:4:66,685] communities.

[3:0:66,68] 0360 - STATE PLANNING AND POLICY DEVELOPMENT  

[4:0:66,86] By statute, the Office is the state comprehensive planning agency. The major activities of the State Planning and Policy  

[4:1:66,96] Development program can be grouped into four major categories: land use and planning, climate risk and resilience,  

[4:2:66,105] sustainable economic development, and targeted long-range research needs. More specifically these include: (1)  

[5:0:66,115] recommending and implementing state policies on land-use and growth planning and compliance with environmental statutes  

[5:1:66,125] and regulations, including General Plan Guidelines and other guidance to local and regional governments; (2) coordinating the  

[5:2:66,135] implementation of the California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA), including: (a) operating the State Clearinghouse; (b)  

[5:3:66,144] maintaining an online database for the electronic submission and archiving of CEQA documents; (c) developing CEQA  

[6:0:66,154] guidelines amendments; (d) providing technical assistance; (e) providing training, and (f) coordinating SB 7 and SB 149 project  

[6:1:66,164] review (3) supporting the Governor's Advisor for Military Affairs and Governor's Military Council; (4) providing policy research  

[6:2:66,174] for the Governor and Cabinet; (5) supporting local planning efforts related to the impacts of droughts and wildfires; (6)  

[6:3:66,183] partnering on the development of state plans including, but not limited to, the Water Action Plan, the State Multi-Hazard  

[6:4:66,193] Mitigation Plan, the State Adaptation Strategy, the Integrated Energy Policy Report, and the 5-Year Infrastructure Plan, as well  

[6:5:66,203] as leading   the California Climate Change Assessment; (7) supporting multiple efforts to address climate change and response  

[6:6:66,213] to carbon pollution; (8) administering the Integrated Climate Adaptation and Resiliency Program to coordinate regional and  

[6:7:66,223] local efforts with state climate adaptation strategies to adapt to the impacts of climate change; (9) housing the Federal Grants  

[6:8:66,232] Administrator for tracking of federal grants coming to California and providing information on federal grants to help maximize  

[6:9:66,242] federal grant opportunities within the state; (10) administering the California Education Learning Lab; (11) implementing the  

[6:10:66,252] Regional Early Action Planning Grants of 2021 (REAP 2.0) which intends to help the state meet its climate commitments and  

[6:11:66,262] housing production affordability goals;   (12) administering the   Racial Equity Commission; and (13) conducting other activities as  

[6:12:66,271] the Governor or Legislature may direct. 

[7:0:66,289] 0370 - CALIFORNIA STRATEGIC GROWTH COUNCIL  

[8:0:66,306] The California Strategic Growth Council (SGC) coordinates and works collaboratively with public agencies, communities, and  

[8:1:66,316] key partners to advance healthy, thriving, and resilient communities for all. SGC integrates state, regional, and local efforts to  

[8:2:66,326] reduce greenhouse gas emissions; increase the availability of affordable housing located near resources like jobs, services,  

[8:3:66,335] and green space; conserve agriculture lands; strengthen community resilience; promote public health; and advance racial  

[8:4:66,345] equity. SGC administers the following grant programs: Affordable Housing and Sustainable Communities; Transformative  

[8:5:66,355] Climate Communities; Sustainable Agricultural Lands Conservation; and SGC’s Community Resilience Centers Program,  

[8:6:66,365] which provides grants to support communities’ ability to withstand climate-related disasters and build resilience year-round  

[8:7:66,374] SGC operates these funding programs in collaboration with interagency teams to develop program guidelines, review  

[9:0:66,384] applications, and administer program funds. SGC’s Community Assistance for Climate Equity Program encompasses both the  

[9:1:66,394] Regional Climate Collaboratives, which supports local capacity building and technical assistance in under-resourced  

[10:0:66,404] communities across California; and the California Climate Investments Technical Assistance Program, which increases access  

[10:1:66,414] to SGC’s own grant programs as well as those of many other State agencies. This program now includes the Tribal Capacity  

[10:2:66,423] Building Program.   SGC’s Health and Equity Program advances the integration of health and equity principles in State programs  

[10:3:66,433] and planning through the Health in All Policies Task Force, partnerships and collaborations, and in the implementation of SGC’s  

[10:4:66,443] Racial Equity Action Plan. SGC administers the Agricultural Land Equity Task Force, a three-year initiative. SGC runs the  

[10:5:66,453] Connecting Communities Initiative, which is designed to connect California Communities to federal and other non-state funding  

[10:6:66,462] programs. Finally, SGC is charged with reviewing the State’s 5-Year Infrastructure Plan and contributing to interagency efforts  

[10:7:66,472] to promote sustainability, equity, and resilience in State investments.

[7:0:121,251] 0680   Governor’s Office of Service and Community Engagement  

[8:0:66,271] The Governor’s Office of Service and Community Engagement (GO SERVE) elevates paid service and volunteerism in the  

[8:1:66,281] state, promotes more youth and community engagement, and advances public awareness and outreach campaigns to tackle  

[8:2:66,291] the state’s most pressing challenges.  

[9:0:66,308] GO SERVE consists of the California Volunteers, the Office of Community Partnerships and Strategic Communications, and the  

[9:1:66,318] Youth Empowerment Commission.   California Volunteers aims to increase the number and impact of Californians involved with  

[9:2:66,328] service and volunteering throughout the state. The Office of Community Partnerships and Strategic Communications  

[9:3:66,338] implements public awareness and community outreach campaigns related to the state’s highest priority issues facing our  

[9:4:66,347] communities. The Youth Empowerment Commission provides meaningful opportunities for civic engagement to improve the  

[9:5:66,357] quality of life for California’s disconnected and disadvantaged youth.  

[10:0:66,374] Chapter 41, Statutes of 2024 (SB 164) established GO SERVE on July 1, 2024, and transferred California Volunteers, the  

[10:1:66,384] Office of Community Partnerships and Strategic Communications and the Youth Empowerment Commission from the  

[10:2:66,394] Governor’s Office of Land Use and Climate Innovation (formerly the Office of Planning and Research) to GO SERVE.

[8:0:66,369] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[9:0:66,388] 0372 -  California Volunteers  

[10:0:66,405] California Volunteers is tasked with engaging Californians in service, volunteering and civic action to tackle the state’s most  

[10:1:66,415] pressing challenges while lifting up all communities. The California Service Corps consists of the CaliforniansForAll College  

[10:2:66,425] Corps, Youth Service Corps, California Climate Action Corps, and AmeriCorps California. From the California Climate Action  

[10:3:66,434] Corps, the country’s first statewide climate corps program, to the CaliforniansForAll service initiative launched in response to  

[10:4:66,444] COVID-19 to establish a volunteer corps to support the state’s response to emergencies and disasters, California Volunteers  

[10:5:66,454] plays an integral role in addressing the state’s problems. California Volunteers is supported by a bipartisan 25-member  

[10:6:66,464] Commission and a team of experts driven by a mission to empower and mobilize all Californians to volunteer and serve in their  

[10:7:66,473] communities.  

[11:0:66,491] California Volunteers also houses the Youth Empowerment Commission that engages youth directly with policymakers  

[11:1:66,501] providing meaningful opportunities for civic engagement to improve the quality of life for California’s underserved and  

[11:2:66,510] marginalized youth. The Commission examines and discusses policy and fiscal issues affecting the interests, needs, and  

[11:3:66,520] conditions of the youth of California, formally advises and makes recommendations to the Legislature, Superintendent of Public  

[11:4:66,530] Instruction, and Governor on specific legislative and fiscal issues affecting youth.  

[12:0:66,547] 0373 -  Office of Community Partnerships and Strategic Communications  

[13:0:66,564] The Office of   Community Partnerships   and Strategic Communications is a   single state entity coordinating California’s most  

[13:1:66,574] important statewide public awareness and community outreach efforts, which   allows the state to realize more inclusive and  

[13:2:66,584] effective outcomes while preventing equity gaps in statewide outreach. With the unprecedented scale of the challenges  

[13:3:66,594] California is facing, the state must be able to communicate effectively with all Californians, including those who are  

[13:4:66,603] experiencing the greatest health and social inequities. The tested model of an ecosystem of trusted messengers builds on the  

[13:5:66,613] success of Census 2020 and Vaccinate ALL 58 campaigns. The Office implements micro-targeted public education and  

[13:6:66,623] communication efforts to benefit under-served Californians. The Office’s tested model of State-CBO outreach collaboration  

[13:7:66,633] employs a result-based management system to: 1) implement data-driven and qualitative analysis for accountability,  

[13:8:66,643] evaluation, and resource allocations; 2) analyze data trends to identify communities of concern and monitor outputs; 3)   fund  

[13:9:66,652] community-based organizations to address access and inclusion through relevant cultural and in-language materials and  

[13:10:66,662] tactics; 4) execute integrated media campaigns to reach targeted populations and collaborating with media, including ethnic  

[13:11:66,672] media, to dispel misinformation; 5) coordinate with state and public agencies, elected representatives, faith-based  

[13:12:66,682] organizations, philanthropy, and other civil society groups to leverage resources and expand impact.  

[14:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[13:0:202,604] 0690   Office of Emergency Services  

[14:0:66,625] The principal objective of the Office of Emergency Services (Cal OES) is to protect lives and property, build emergency  

[14:1:66,635] response capabilities, and support communities for a resilient California. The Cal OES Director serves as both the Governor's  

[14:2:66,645] Homeland Security Advisor and Emergency Management Director, with responsibility to implement and facilitate the state's  

[14:3:66,654] homeland security and counter-terrorism strategy. Cal OES serves the public through effective collaboration in preparing for,  

[14:4:66,664] protecting against, responding to, recovering from, and mitigating the impacts of hazards and threats.  

[14:5:66,681] Cal OES provides leadership, assistance, training, and support to state and local agencies and coordinates with federal  

[14:6:66,691] agencies in planning and preparing for the most effective use of federal, state, local, and private sector resources in  

[14:7:66,701] emergencies. This emergency planning is based upon a system of mutual aid whereby a jurisdiction relies first on its own  

[15:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[0:0:66,13] LEGISLATIVE, JUDICIAL, AND EXECUTIVE 

[1:0:410,13] 2024-25 STATE BUDGET — LJE   115 

[2:0:167,32] 0690   Office of Emergency Services - Continued 

[3:0:66,68] resources, and then requests assistance from its neighbors. Cal OES' plans and programs are coordinated with those of the  

[3:1:66,78] federal government, other states, private sector, utilities, and state and local agencies within California.  

[4:0:66,96] During an emergency, Cal OES functions as the Governor's immediate staff to provide guidance and coordinate the state's  

[4:1:66,105] responsibilities under the Emergency Services Act and applicable federal statutes. It also acts as the conduit for federal  

[4:2:66,115] assistance through natural disaster grants and federal agency support. Additionally, Cal OES is responsible for the  

[4:3:66,125] development and coordination of a comprehensive state strategy related to all hazards, including terrorism, which includes  

[4:4:66,135] prevention, preparedness, mitigation, response, and recovery.  

[5:0:66,152] Cal OES implements the state's homeland security strategy by overseeing the California Cybersecurity Integration Center and  

[5:1:66,162] the State Threat Assessment System (STAS), which includes management of the State Threat Assessment Center. The STAS  

[5:2:66,171] assists in the detection, prevention, and investigation of   and response to criminal and terrorist activity and   also facilitates  

[5:3:66,181] information and intelligence sharing between local, state, federal, tribal agencies, and private sector partners.  

[6:0:66,198] The Alfred E. Alquist Seismic Safety   Commission   is a separate unit within the   Office of Emergency Services. Its mission is to  

[6:1:66,208] lower earthquake risk to life and property of Californians. The Commission works with federal, state, and local agencies, as well  

[6:2:66,218] as the private sector, on a variety of activities that guide and stimulate earthquake risk reduction and management.  

[7:0:66,235] Because Cal OES' programs drive a need for infrastructure investment, Cal OES has a capital outlay program to support this  

[7:1:66,245] need. For the specifics on Cal OES' capital outlay program, see "Infrastructure Overview."

[0:0:66,13] LEGISLATIVE, JUDICIAL, AND EXECUTIVE 

[1:0:410,13] 2024-25 STATE BUDGET — LJE   121 

[2:0:167,32] 0690   Office of Emergency Services - Continued 

[3:0:66,65] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[4:0:66,84] 0380 - EMERGENCY MANAGEMENT SERVICES  

[5:0:66,103] Working through the state's mutual aid system, the Emergency Management Services and Homeland Security Program  

[5:1:66,113] coordinates the provision   of federal, state, and local resources to jurisdictions whose resources and services are overextended  

[5:2:66,123] in a disaster situation. In addition, this program develops and coordinates a comprehensive state strategy related to an all-

[5:3:66,133] hazards approach that includes prevention, preparedness, mitigation, response, and recovery consistent with the National  

[5:4:66,142] Strategy on Homeland Security. Central to this effort is maintaining operational readiness at all levels of government. Within this  

[5:5:66,152] program, Cal OES also trains emergency managers, responders, and state and local leaders in preparedness and response to  

[5:6:66,162] all hazards.  

[6:0:66,179] 0385 - SPECIAL PROGRAMS AND GRANT MANAGEMENT  

[7:0:66,196] Cal OES serves as the State Administering Agent for federal homeland security, emergency management, and victim services  

[7:1:66,206] grants and is the primary liaison with the Federal Emergency Management Agency, the United States Department of Homeland  

[7:2:66,216] Security, and other federal agencies. Additionally, Cal OES serves as an advocate for local public safety, emergency  

[7:3:66,226] management, and public and private agencies operating public safety and victim service programs. As part of its grant  

[7:4:66,236] management role, Cal OES administers the California Disaster Assistance Act and provides eligible local agencies with  

[7:5:66,245] financial assistance to recover from disasters. Included in this program is the State Threat Assessment Center, which is the  

[7:6:66,255] centerpiece of the state's intelligence information sharing environment and serves as the Governor's designated primary fusion  

[7:7:66,265] center.  

[8:0:66,282] 0390 - ALFRED E. ALQUIST SEISMIC SAFETY COMMISSION  

[9:0:66,299] The Alfred E. Alquist Seismic Safety Commission program provides a coordinated framework for establishing consistent  

[9:1:66,309] earthquake policies; advising the Governor, the Legislature, local governments, and the public; and tracking the state’s  

[9:2:66,319] progress toward higher levels of seismic safety.   The Commission uses the expertise of its commissioners to review, evaluate,  

[9:3:66,329] and translate scientific information and make recommendations to guide and influence earthquake safety policies.   The  

[9:4:66,339] Commission works with federal, state, and local agencies, as well as the private sector, on a variety of activities that support  

[9:5:66,348] the state’s earthquake preparedness, mitigation, response, and recovery efforts.   These activities include: (1) developing and  

[9:6:66,358] reviewing seismic safety projects; (2) providing consistent policy direction; (3) proposing and reviewing earthquake-related  

[9:7:66,368] legislation; (4) conducting public hearings on seismic safety issues; (5) using existing knowledge and conducting studies,  

[9:8:66,378] where necessary, to improve the performance of structures in California, (6) recommending earthquake safety programs and  

[9:9:66,387] supporting cost-effective partnerships that help reduce earthquake risks and speed economic recovery.  

[9:10:66,405] 0395 - PUBLIC SAFETY COMMUNICATIONS  

[10:0:66,424] The Public Safety Communications   program is responsible for the design, installation, maintenance, and repair of the  

[10:1:66,434] state's   public safety communications networks and oversight of the state's 9-1-1 system. The   program is dedicated to the  

[10:2:66,444] preservation and protection of human life and public safety by delivering reliable and dependable communication services that  

[10:3:66,454] keep the public connected during times of crisis.  

[10:4:66,471] 9900 - ADMINISTRATION AND EXECUTIVE  

[11:0:66,490] The Administration and Executive Program provides the overall policy direction of   Cal OES and support services such as  

[11:1:66,500] accounting, fiscal, personnel, information technology, and business services.

[11:1:66,552] Regional Operations Center in Sacramento County; a Coastal Regional Operations Center in Fairfield in Solano County; a

[11:3:66,571] Obispo; and various small field offices throughout the state.

[12:1:66,599] throughout the state. These locations include 7 area offices and 41 area shops, positioned geographically to facilitate  

[12:2:66,608] maintenance and installation services to remote communication sites and customers throughout the state. In addition, the PSC  

[12:3:66,618] maintains and operates 11 communications vaults/towers and a total of more than 3,500 radio frequency points of presence.

[11:0:191,663] 0750   Office of the Lieutenant Governor  

[12:0:66,684] Under California's Constitution, the Lieutenant Governor serves as Acting Governor whenever the Governor is absent from the  

[12:1:66,694] state, and automatically becomes Governor if a vacancy occurs in the Office of Governor. The Lieutenant Governor is also  

[12:2:66,704] President of the Senate and votes in case of a tie.

[3:0:66,68] The Lieutenant Governor serves as a voting member of the Board of Regents of the University of California, the Board of  

[3:1:66,78] Trustees of the California State University system, and the Board of Governors of the California Community Colleges system.  

[3:2:66,88] The Lieutenant Governor also sits on the Calbright College Board of Trustees.  

[4:0:66,105] The Lieutenant Governor also serves on, and rotates with the State Controller, as chair of the three-member State Lands  

[4:1:66,115] Commission, which oversees the control and leasing of millions of acres of state-owned land, including offshore oil resources,  

[4:2:66,125] as well as use and permitting for all navigable waterways in California. The Commission also manages state land-use planning  

[4:3:66,135] and revenues, and related interstate issues. During alternate years, when the Lieutenant Governor serves as Chairperson of  

[4:4:66,144] the State Lands Commission, the Lieutenant Governor also serves as a member of the Ocean Protection Council   and as a  

[4:5:66,154] non-voting member of the California Coastal Commission.  

[5:0:66,171] In addition, under state statutes, the Lieutenant Governor chairs the California Commission for Economic Development, which  

[5:1:66,181] provides support and guidance to the Governor, Legislature, and private sector regarding the development of California's  

[5:2:66,191] economy.

[6:0:66,511] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[6:1:66,530] 0435 - LEGAL SERVICES  

[7:0:66,550] Legal Services is organized into five elements: (1) Civil Law, (2) Criminal Law, (3) Public Rights, (4) Medi-Cal and Elder Abuse,  

[7:1:66,559] and (5) Office of General Counsel.  

[8:0:66,579] Civil Law represents the State of California and its officers, agencies, departments, boards, commissions, and employees in  

[8:1:66,589] civil matters. It provides advice to these clients, defends cases brought against them, prosecutes cases to vindicate state  

[8:2:66,599] interests, and conducts investigations. Deputy Attorneys General in Civil Law are responsible for managing and litigating cases  

[8:3:66,608] before administrative tribunals, and in both state and federal courts at the trial level and on appeal, including appeals before the  

[8:4:66,618] United States and California Supreme Courts. Deputies work in one of nine sections: Business Litigation; Cannabis Control;  

[8:5:66,628] Correctional Law; Employment Law; Government Law; Health, Education, and Welfare; Health Quality Enforcement; Licensing;  

[8:6:66,638] and Tort and Condemnation.  

[9:0:66,657] Criminal Law represents the   People of the State of California   in criminal matters before the appellate and Supreme Courts.  

[9:1:66,667] Criminal Law also fulfills the Attorney General's responsibilities of assisting district attorneys in cases for which they are  

[9:2:66,677] recused, conducting criminal investigations, representing the Governor, Board of Parole Hearings, and California Department of  

[9:3:66,687] Corrections and Rehabilitation in state and federal habeas corpus cases and appeals, and other proceedings relating to parole  

[9:4:66,696] decisions and conditions of confinement in the state prisons, and defending criminal judgements in state and federal habeas  

[9:5:66,706] corpus matters. Additional responsibilities include enforcing the Political Reform Act, advising the Governor on extradition  

[9:6:66,716] matters, and investigating, prosecuting, and coordinating litigation involving white-collar crimes, high-tech/computer/privacy  

[10:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[0:0:66,13] LEGISLATIVE, JUDICIAL, AND EXECUTIVE 

[1:0:410,13] 2024-25 STATE BUDGET — LJE   139 

[2:0:189,32] 0820   Department of Justice - Continued 

[3:0:66,68] crimes, financial crimes, human trafficking, environmental crimes, public corruption, and officer-involved shootings. The newly  

[3:1:66,78] created Post-Conviction Justice Unit is charged with handling matters involving resentencing and conviction review.  

[4:0:66,98] Public Rights protects and preserves the public’s interests by providing legal services to state agencies, boards and  

[4:1:66,108] commissions, and Constitutional Officers, and by bringing actions in the name of the Attorney General on behalf of the People  

[4:2:66,117] to protect the public. Public Rights provides specialized services in the following areas: Antitrust Law, Nonprofit and Charitable  

[4:3:66,127] Trust Enforcement and Regulation (including the Registry of Charities and Fundraisers); Civil Rights Enforcement (including the  

[4:4:66,137] Bureaus of Children's Justice, Racial Justice, and Disability Rights); Consumer Protection (including Privacy Enforcement and  

[4:5:66,147] Sellers of Travel); Corporate Fraud (including False Claims and Corporate Responsibility); Environment (including the Bureau  

[4:6:66,156] of Environmental Justice); Healthcare Rights and Access (including Tobacco, Reproductive Rights, Health Equity, Hospital  

[4:7:66,166] Transactions, and Healthcare Competition and Consumer Protection); Native American and Tribal Affairs; Natural Resources  

[4:8:66,176] Law; Land Use and Conservation; Police Practices; and Worker Rights and Fair Labor.  

[5:0:66,193] The Division of Medi-Cal Fraud and Elder Abuse represents the People of the State of California in both criminal and civil  

[5:1:66,203] matters involving Medi-Cal provider fraud, and the abuse or neglect of elder and dependent adults and Medi-Cal recipients.  

[5:2:66,213] The Division is a vertical prosecution unit whose investigations are conducted by multidisciplinary teams consisting of Special  

[5:3:66,223] Agents, Investigative Auditors, Digital Forensic Specialists, Registered Nurses, and Deputy Attorneys General. Deputy  

[5:4:66,232] Attorneys General from the Division represent the People of the State of California in both federal and state courts. Types of  

[5:5:66,242] cases frequently prosecuted by the Division include fraud committed against the Medi-Cal program by doctors, pharmacies,  

[5:6:66,252] clinics, dentists, medical equipment suppliers, hospice, home health companies, and all other Medi-Cal providers; elder or  

[5:7:66,262] dependent adult abuse or neglect in skilled nursing facilities, residential care facilities for the elderly, intermediate care facilities  

[5:8:66,271] for the developmentally disabled, and other specified residential care facilities; and the neglect or abuse of Medi-Cal recipients  

[5:9:66,281] in non-institutional settings, when such abuse or neglect is connected to the provision of case.  

[6:0:66,299] The Office of General Counsel serves as a single point of contact for legal advice to the Department of Justice’s various  

[6:1:66,308] programs and bureaus, as well as coordinates and oversees legal compliance and risk-management efforts across the  

[6:2:66,318] Department. Key areas of legal work include information security and data storage and disclosure; law-enforcement operations;  

[6:3:66,328] contracting, agreements, and grants; professional ethics; financial conflicts and other government ethics requirements;  

[6:4:66,338] regulations; the Public Records Act; the Administrative Procedure Act; the Bagley-Keene Act’s open meeting requirements; and  

[6:5:66,347] public finance. Attorneys within this division also lead or support internal investigations, operational projects that further  

[6:6:66,357] Departmental risk-management and compliance missions, and the development and implementation of policies and procedures  

[6:7:66,367] within the Department. Also within the Office of General Counsel are the Office of Program Oversight and Accountability, as  

[6:8:66,377] well as the Office of Information Security and Research Services, which provides cybersecurity direction and policy guidance  

[6:9:66,386] on information security and privacy matters, and research services for the Department.  

[7:0:66,404] 0440 - LAW ENFORCEMENT  

[8:0:66,423] The Division of Law Enforcement is organized into five areas: (1) Bureau of Firearms, (2) Bureau of Forensic Services, (3)  

[8:1:66,433] Bureau of Gambling Control, (4) Bureau of Investigation, and (5) the Office of the Chief.  

[9:0:66,453] The Bureau of Firearms (BOF) implements and enforces California's firearms and ammunition   laws by administering a  

[9:1:66,462] multitude of different state-mandated firearms and ammunition-related programs. This is accomplished by conducting firearm  

[9:2:66,472] and ammunition eligibility checks, conducting compliance inspections of firearm dealers, ammunition vendors, and  

[9:3:66,482] manufacturers, and by providing valuable training to stakeholders statewide. BOF Special Agents conduct investigations into  

[9:4:66,492] armed and prohibited persons and other investigations resulting in the seizure of firearms, magazines, and ammunition. Finally,  

[9:5:66,501] BOF Special Agents conduct investigations to monitor and   prevent illegal   firearms trafficking at permitted gun shows in  

[9:6:66,511] accordance with state and federal laws.  

[10:0:66,531] The Bureau of Forensic Services (BFS) provides evaluation and scientific analysis of physical evidence, crime scene  

[10:1:66,541] investigation, and scientific investigative support for officer-involved shooting investigations. Additionally BFS provides expert  

[10:2:66,550] court testimony to federal, state and local law enforcement agencies, district attorneys, and courts. BFS operates 10 regional  

[10:3:66,560] crime laboratories and two specialized laboratories, the Jan Bashinski DNA Laboratory, and the Statewide Toxicology  

[10:4:66,570] Laboratory. These laboratories serve 46 of California’s 58 counties. BFS also operates the California Criminalistics Institute  

[10:5:66,580] forensic training facility that provides training for forensic scientists worldwide. Finally, BFS maintains the state DNA database,  

[10:6:66,589] which stores and regularly searches the DNA profiles of sex and violent offenders and felony arrestees against the DNA  

[10:7:66,599] profiles of evidence from unsolved crimes.  

[11:0:66,619] The Bureau of Gambling Control (BGC) regulates California cardrooms and tribal casinos to ensure gambling is conducted  

[11:1:66,629] honestly and is free from criminal and corruptive elements. This is accomplished by investigating the qualifications of  

[11:2:66,638] individuals and business entities who apply for licenses and by monitoring the conduct of these licensees to ensure compliance  

[11:3:66,648] with the Gambling Control Act and applicable regulations. BGC also encompasses an audit component to ensure solvency in  

[11:4:66,658] gambling establishments and provides investigative audit expertise. BGC conducts criminal investigations in and around tribal  

[11:5:66,668] casinos and California cardrooms. In addition, BGC conducts Compact Compliance reviews for tribal gaming to ensure that  

[11:6:66,677] each tribe is in compliance with all aspects of the state gaming compact.  

[12:0:66,697] The Bureau of Investigation (BI) investigates and dismantles criminal organizations and assists with the prosecution of serious  

[12:1:66,707] criminal offenses that present a significant and multi-jurisdictional threat to California. BI prioritizes investigations related to  

[13:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.
