[6:0:66,248] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[6:1:66,267] 0895 - CALIFORNIA ABLE ACT BOARD  

[7:0:66,286] On December 19, 2014, President Obama signed the Stephen Beck Jr., Achieving a Better Life Experience Act, which allows  

[7:1:66,296] individuals who became blind or disabled before reaching age 26, to create tax-free savings accounts. Chapter 774, Statutes of  

[7:2:66,306] 2015 (AB 449), implements the ABLE Act in California, and directs the Board to administer the California ABLE Program.  

[8:0:66,326] The Board and the California ABLE Program Trust were established by Chapter 796, Statutes of 2015 (SB 324), for the  

[8:1:66,335] purpose of creating the Program. CalABLE was officially launched in December of 2018 with the mission to meet the diverse  

[8:2:66,345] needs of ABLE customers and their families. CalABLE’s pledge is to be customer-driven, accountable, and a trusted partner in  

[8:3:66,355] providing financial services.  

[9:0:66,372] Under the Program, a person may make contributions of up to $18,000 during a taxable year, to a designated beneficiary's  

[9:1:66,382] ABLE account. Funds may accumulate and grow in CalABLE investments with no federal or state income taxes or penalties if  

[9:2:66,392] the contributions are used to pay for qualified expenses. Funds up to $100,000 held in the ABLE account also do not affect  

[9:3:66,401] eligibility for Supplemental Security Income (SSI) disability benefits, which without an ABLE account limit accumulated assets  

[9:4:66,411] of beneficiaries to $2,000.  

[10:0:66,429] In 2022, Governor Newsom signed AB 2216 into law, limiting state protections from Medi-Cal recovery upon the death of an  

[10:1:66,438] ABLE beneficiary, only to CalABLE account holders, and permitting CalABLE account holders who are working to contribute up  

[10:2:66,448] to the full amount allowable under the federal ABLE to Work provision. In 2023, the Governor signed AB 339 into law,  

[10:3:66,458] expanding eligibility to open a CalABLE account to individuals whose disability began before age 46. This law conforms with a  

[10:4:66,468] change in federal law and will go into effect in 2026.

[12:0:181,537] 0984   CalSavers Retirement Savings Board  

[13:0:66,558] The   CalSavers Retirement Savings Board (Board) was established by Chapter 734, Statutes of 2012 (SB 1234). Chapter 804,  

[13:1:66,568] Statutes of 2016 (SB 1234), subsequently authorized the Board to implement the CalSavers Retirement Savings Program  

[13:2:66,578] (CalSavers), a state-administered retirement savings program for private sector employees in California with no access to  

[13:3:66,587] workplace retirement savings plans. The Board’s mission is to ensure all Californians have a path to financial security in  

[13:4:66,597] retirement by providing a simple, portable, low-cost way for workers to invest in their futures.  

[14:0:66,614] The Board consists of nine members: the State Treasurer (Chairperson), the Director of the Department of Finance, the State  

[14:1:66,624] Controller, a retirement savings and investment expert appointed by the Senate Committee on Rules, an employee  

[14:2:66,634] representative appointed by the Speaker of the Assembly, a small business representative appointed by the Governor, a public  

[14:3:66,644] member appointed by the Governor, and two additional members appointed by the Governor.

[11:0:66,508] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[11:1:66,527] 0910 - CALSAVERS  

[12:0:66,544] The Program provides workers access to a simple, portable, low-cost retirement savings account. Any private sector employer  

[12:1:66,554] with at least one employee that does not offer a workplace retirement savings vehicle by the statutory compliance deadline, or  

[12:2:66,564] is otherwise exempted, is required to provide their employees with access to the Program. The final compliance deadline for  

[12:3:66,573] employers with five or more employees was June 30, 2022. Following the passage of SB 1126 in 2022, the compliance  

[12:4:66,583] deadline for employers with less than five employees is December 31, 2025.

[4:0:185,140] 0985   California School Finance Authority  

[5:0:66,161] The California School Finance Authority (CSFA), created in 1985, provides facilities and working capital financing to school  

[5:1:66,171] districts, community college districts, county offices of education, and charter schools. The State Treasurer serves as chair of  

[5:2:66,180] CSFA, and the Superintendent of Public Instruction and the Director of Finance serve as members. CSFA has offices in Los  

[5:3:66,190] Angeles and Sacramento.  

[6:0:66,207] CSFA serves as the primary state agency for California charter schools seeking facility and working capital funding through  

[6:1:66,217] several state and federally funded programs.

[8:0:66,382] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[9:0:66,401] 0918 - SMART BONDS PROGRAM  

[10:0:66,420] Chapter 1438, Statutes of 1985, as amended by Chapter 598, Statutes of 1987, established CSFA and authorized the issuance  

[10:1:66,430] of revenue bonds or other debt instruments. The proceeds from the sale of the bonds are available for loans to schools and  

[10:2:66,440] community college districts to assist with the acquisition of equipment and new school sites, construction of new facilities,  

[10:3:66,450] reconstruction of existing facilities, capital improvements, and to provide working capital. Chapter 325, Statutes of 2006 (AB  

[10:4:66,459] 2717), allows CSFA to issue debt on behalf of California charter schools for capital improvements and working capital needs.  

[11:0:66,477] 0920 - CHARTER SCHOOL FACILITIES PROGRAM  

[12:0:66,496] Chapter 935, Statutes of 2002, as amended by Chapter 587, Statutes of 2003, created the Charter School Facilities Program  

[12:1:66,506] (CSFP), which provides funding for the new construction, renovation or rehabilitation of charter school facilities. CSFA and the  

[12:2:66,516] Office of Public School Construction jointly administer the program. CSFP was funded through the Kindergarten-University  

[12:3:66,525] Public Education Facilities Bond Acts of 2002, 2004, 2006, and 2016, for a total of $1.4 billion. The program provides a 50  

[12:4:66,535] percent state subsidy for charter school facilities project costs, with the balance of the project costs being repaid (to the state)  

[12:5:66,545] by the charter school via a 30-year loan. Recipient charter schools must provide site-based instruction, be financially sound,  

[12:6:66,555] and meet other program eligibility requirements. 

[13:0:66,572] 0925 - STATE CHARTER SCHOOL FACILITIES INCENTIVE GRANTS PROGRAM  

[14:0:66,589] In 2004, 2009, and 2014, CSFA received grants under the United States Department of Education’s State Charter School  

[14:1:66,599] Facilities Incentive Grants Program (CFDA 84.282D) to provide California charter schools with assistance for facilities costs.  

[14:2:66,609] Grant funds reimburse a charter school’s costs for rent, lease, mortgage or debt service payments for existing or new facilities  

[14:3:66,619] or the costs of acquiring land and/or constructing or renovating a facility. Grants are awarded to charter schools based on  

[14:4:66,628] preference points assigned based on: the percentage of low-income students; percentage of overcrowding; not-for-profit status;  

[14:5:66,638] and demonstrated student performance. Schools cannot use program funds to supplant state funding. This program sunset in  

[14:6:66,648] December 2022.  

[15:0:66,665] 0930 - CHARTER SCHOOL FACILITY GRANT PROGRAM  

[16:0:66,683] The Charter School Facility Grant Program provides Proposition 98 General Fund grants to assist charter schools with rent and  

[16:1:66,692] lease costs. This program targets schools and communities with significant populations of economically disadvantaged  

[16:2:66,702] students. Eligible charter schools are provided the lesser of $1,432 per unit of eligible average daily attendance, or 75 percent  

[16:3:66,712] of annual facilities rent and lease costs.  

[17:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[3:0:66,68] 0935 - CHARTER SCHOOL REVOLVING LOAN FUND  

[3:1:66,86] Charter 1010, Statutes of 1976 established the Charter School Revolving Loan Fund in the State Treasury to provide loans of  

[3:2:66,96] up to $250,000 to new charter schools to assist them in meeting the purposes of the school's approved charter. The program is  

[3:3:66,105] available to any charter school that is not a conversion of an existing public school, and preference goes to schools that have  

[3:4:66,115] not opened nor completed their full charter term.  

[3:5:66,132] 0938 - STUDENT HOUSING REVOLVING LOAN PROGRAM 

[3:6:66,150] Chapter 572, Statutes of 2022 established the California Student Housing Revolving Loan Fund, which provides zero-interest  

[3:7:66,159] loans for affordable student, faculty, and staff housing.

[10:0:168,500] 0989   California Educational Facilities Authority  

[11:0:66,521] The California Educational Facilities Authority (CEFA) provides assistance to qualified nonprofit higher education institutions  

[11:1:66,531] through a tax-exempt revenue bond program to reduce the costs of financing academic facilities.  

[12:0:66,548] CEFA consists of the following five members: the Director of Finance, the State Controller, the State Treasurer, and two public  

[12:1:66,558] members appointed by the Governor.

[10:0:66,525] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[10:1:66,543] 0940 - BOND FINANCING  

[11:0:66,561] CEFA issues tax-exempt revenue bonds to assist private educational institutions of higher learning to construct educational  

[11:1:66,570] facilities. Because it is authorized to issue tax-exempt bonds, CEFA may be able to provide more favorable financing terms  

[11:2:66,580] than might otherwise be obtainable. CEFA also may include qualifying nonprofit entities as eligible program participants for the  

[11:3:66,590] construction of student and faculty housing. Bonds issued by CEFA are not a debt, liability, or claim on the faith and credit or  

[11:4:66,600] the taxing power of the State of California or any of its political subdivisions. The full faith and credit of the participating  

[11:5:66,609] institution is pledged to the payment of the bonds. Bonds issued for this purpose are not subject to the state's "private activity"  

[11:6:66,619] bond ceiling as specified in federal law.  

[12:0:66,648] For purposes of the California Educational Facilities Act, "private college" or "participating private college" means a nonprofit,  

[12:1:66,658] private, regionally accredited, degree-granting college that does not restrict the admission of a student based on the student's  

[12:2:66,668] race or ethnicity and provided that the financing does not violate constitutional provisions.  

[13:0:66,697] "Bond" means bonds, notes, debentures, securities, or other evidences of indebtedness. This broad definition allows CEFA to  

[14:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[3:1:66,78] than these colleges and universities might otherwise realize on a traditional bond financing.  

[4:0:66,98] 0951 - STUDENT HOUSING REVOLVING LOAN PROGRAM  

[5:0:66,115] Chapter 572, Statutes of 2022, established the California Student Housing Revolving Loan Fund (CaSH RLF), which provides  

[5:1:66,125] zero-interest loans for affordable student housing and affordable faculty and staff housing.  

[6:0:66,152] 0955 - COLLEGE ACCESS TAX CREDIT FUND  

[7:0:66,169] Chapter 367, Statutes of 2014, required CEFA to administer the College Access Tax Credit Fund and allocate and certify the  

[7:1:66,179] tax credits for taxable years beginning on or after January 1, 2014, and before January 1, 2017. Chapter 22, Statutes of 2015,  

[7:2:66,189] added a requirement that CEFA continue to allocate and certify the tax credits for taxable years beginning on or after January  

[7:3:66,198] 1, 2017, and before January 1, 2018. Chapter 527, Statutes of 2017, extended CEFA's responsibility to administer the tax  

[7:4:66,208] credits for taxable years beginning on or after January 1, 2017, and before January 1, 2023.   Chapter 976, Statues of 2022,  

[7:5:66,218] extended CEFA’s responsibility further to taxable years beginning before January 1, 2028.   Chapter 278, Statutes of 2023,  

[7:6:66,228] altered the target student population that the Fund could benefit from students that receive Cal Grant B awards to qualifying  

[7:7:66,237] community college student transfers to regionally accredited Historically Black Colleges and Universities that have an associate  

[7:8:66,247] degree for transfer memorandum of understanding on file with the office of the Chancellor of the California Community  

[7:9:66,257] Colleges.
